The present invention relates to test systems based on transmembrane receptors from helminth and arthropods, and to identify and characterize substances acting on helminths, arthropods or on the calcium balance of biological host cells. The use of this test system. The invention furthermore relates to the use of a specific ligand in the present test system, and to the use of the ligand as an anthelmintic or arthropodidic active.
[0002]
Parasitic helminths and arthropods are a significant human and animal health problem. In the agricultural sector alone, the cost of combating or preventing the damage caused by such parasites totals more than 7 billion German marks annually (statistics from 1997). A number of active substances belonging to a number of active substance classes are used to treat endoparasites caused mainly by helminths and ectoparasites mainly caused by arthropods. Have been. During the last two decades, it has expanded to a number of parasite species within the phylum (eg, helminths) or to a range of various zoological phyla (eg, helminths and insects). Even so, the importance of active substances which simultaneously exhibit a very good effect is particularly increasing. In particular, the former include broad-spectrum anthelmintics, such as benzimidazole or imidazothiazole, and the latter include macrocyclic lactones.
[0003]
Last time, a group of new, broadly active active substances was on the market about 20 years ago, which was a macrocyclic lactone. However, many endogenous and exogenous parasite species have acquired resistance to individual and, in some cases, simultaneously various classes of active agents. Therefore, the need to develop new substances with anthelmintic activity continues and the urgency is increasing.
[0004]
A few promising new groups of currently active active substances include the cyclic depsipeptides which have been the subject of numerous patents (WO 93/19053, EP 626 376, WO 94/19334, WO 95/07272, EP 626 375, EP 657). 171, EP 657 172, EP 657 173) and their activity has been investigated (Conder et al., 1995; Martin et al., 1996; Sasaki et al., 1992; Terada M 1992; Samson-Himmelstjerna et al., 2000).
[0005]
One representative of this group of actives, PF 1022A (cyclo (-D-Lac-L-MeLeu-D-PhLac-L-MeLeu-)2Many studies have already been described to elucidate the mechanism of action of () (for reference, the relevant information in DE-A-197 04 024). These describe the identification and characterization of DNA sequences encoding binding proteins specific for cyclic depsipeptides and proteins derived from the sheep parasite Haemonchus contortus (DE-A-197 04 024). Was. Within the scope of the present invention, the functional interaction of the protein referred to as HC110-R, in particular the ligand BAY 44-4400 (cyclo (-D-Lac-L-MeLeu-Dp) as a further representative of cyclic depsipeptides Functional interaction with morpholinyl-PhLac-L-MeLeu-), for which purpose HC110-R is converted to HC110-R based on SEQ ID NO: 2 described in the earlier application DE-A-197 04 024. A expressing recombinant eukaryotic cell line was constructed.
[0006]
The present invention therefore relates to the invention, in particular from helminths and arthropods, preferably from nematodes and mites, particularly preferably from ciliate nematodes (Trichostrongylidae), even more preferably from Haemonchus spp. Transmembrane receptors of particular origin include H. It is an object of the present invention to provide a test system capable of high-speed, high-throughput treatment of a test compound (high-throughput screening assay; HTS assay) based on the H. contortus-derived receptor HC110-R.
[0007]
The homologous protein comprises at least 20, preferably at least 25, particularly preferably at least 20, the sequence shown in SEQ ID NO: 2 described in the document DE-A-197 04 024 (the teachings of this document are included in the present application). It is a protein that is at least 70%, preferably 80%, particularly preferably 90%, more preferably 95% identical over its entire length, and more particularly preferably over its entire length.
[0008]
Preferably, amino acid sequence identity is determined using the GAP program of the default GCG program package, version 9.1 (Devereux et al., 1984).
[0009]
It is an object of the present invention to provide polypeptides that exert at least one biological activity of the GPC receptor, and to provide methods for obtaining these polypeptides, as well as nematicidal and arthropodic activities This is achieved by providing a method for identifying a compound having
[0010]
Test systems based on recombinant microorganisms have already been used in many places to identify pharmaceutically active substances, and in particular also microorganisms which recombinantly express parasite genes (Klein and Geary). 1997). However, a system using a parasite transmembrane receptor as a target in a eukaryote as a recombinant functional protein has not been disclosed so far. The test system described in the present invention can be used to identify new classes of receptors in high-throughput-screening (HTS) or ultra-HTS.
[0011]
It is usually difficult to recombinantly express a nematode-derived receptor. Thus, it is currently generally not possible to express a G protein-coupled receptor (GPCR) from a nematode in a manner such that its functional properties (eg, sensitivity to inhibitors) correspond to those of the natural receptor. It is.
[0012]
The functional expression of helminths, especially nematode-derived, and arthropod-derived receptors in eukaryotic systems has proved to be extremely practical in the search for new anthelmintic or arthropodicides, for example. is important.
[0013]
Accordingly, the present invention further aims to provide a method capable of expressing a transmembrane receptor, in particular a GPC receptor from nematodes and arthropods. It is based on developing a test system that can identify new substances with foot activity.
[0014]
Accordingly, the invention is particularly directed to helminths and arthropods, preferably to nematodes and mites, particularly preferably to ciliate nematodes, even more preferably to torsion stomachs, and most preferably to parasitic nematodes H. The present invention relates to expressing and using an orphan G protein-coupled receptor from C. contortus as a target protein for efficient search for nematicidal actives.
[0015]
This receptor is designated G. elegans H. Identification was performed using a cDNA library obtained from C. contortus. The cDNA is a nematode transmembrane protein having a size of 110 kDa and encodes a transmembrane protein called HC110-R. This protein belongs to the secretin family of G protein-coupled receptors (GPCRs) and shows high similarity to latrophilin (FIG. 5).
[0016]
HC110-R receptor as target
GPCR latrophilin was uniquely isolated from mammalian brain. Latrophilin has a molecular weight of 210 kDa and undergoes post-translational cleavage 18 residues upstream of the first transmembrane segment, and is thus composed of two non-covalent subunits. The p120 subunit contains an N-terminal hydrophilic extracellular protein and the p85 subunit contains a seven transmembrane domain and the intracellular C-terminal region of latrophilin, which is unusually large for GPCRs. Two close homologs, latrophilin-2 and latrophilin-3, were recently identified (see also FIG. 6). The latter is preferentially expressed in the brain like latrophilin-1, whereas latrophilin-2 is preferentially expressed ubiquitously in mammalian placenta, kidney, spleen, ovary, heart and lung. (Ichtchenko et al., 1999; Sugita et al., 1998).
[0017]
Although HC110-R is only half the size of latrophilin 210 kDa, sequence similarity extends to functional similarity. Although endogenous ligands for both receptors are not yet known, both latrophilin and HC110-R are known to be affected by the artificial ligand α-LTX (α-latrotoxin).
[0018]
For example, when HEK-293 cells are transiently transfected with latrophilin, radioactive45Ca2+As can be shown by the experimental design using α-LTX, addition of external Ca2+Cause influx. Furthermore, α-LTX was also found to be Ca2 + in HEK-293 cells transiently transfected with HC110-R.2+Cause an influx, which, for example,2+Observable by imaging) (see also FIGS. 10 and 11).
[0019]
However, this Ca2+The inflow is very complex. When HC110-R is in the form of a construct with a C-terminally attached green fluorescent protein (GFP), the influx is biphasic. That is, one change is seen after about 3 minutes and another is seen after about 22 minutes. However, if there is only an N-terminal Myc-His tag before HC110-R, the main influx is only observed about 2-3 minutes after the addition of α-LTX. Although the reason for this is not yet known, the response to α-LTX addition is specific as shown by the following explanation:
1. Ca2+Influx was from untransfected cells and mouse β2-Not observed in cells transiently transfected with adrenergic receptors.
2. [Ca2+]iChanges depend on the dose of α-LTX (FIG. 10).
3. Biphasic changes include Cd as evidenced by their sensitivity to nifedipine2+Ca that can be blocked by2+Ca occurring through channels, especially L-type channels2+It needs to be an inflow.
[0020]
The exact mechanism of interaction and signaling between α-LTX and HC110-R requires further explanation. For the example of latrophilin-1, Ca into HEK-293 cells caused by α-LTX2+It is possible to demonstrate that only a single transmembrane domain is required for influx (Kraspernov et al., 1999).
[0021]
The fact that nifedipine blocks the effects of α-LTX in the system described herein indicates that the system is also suitable for identifying novel specific calcium channel blockers (blockers). Is shown. Nifedipine belongs to the class of calcium channel agonists and antagonists, which are classified on the basis of binding to specific sites of the calcium channel, for example binding to L-type channels. The three major classes of calcium channel blockers (L type) include benzylacetonitrile (eg, verapamil, WO 91/02497), benzothiazepinones (eg, diltiazem), and 1,4 -There are dihydropyridine derivatives (e.g. nifedipine, nivaldipine, nimodipine, nicardipine, isradipine, amlodipine, nitrendipine, felodipine or nisoldipine) (Bacon et al., 1989; WO 90/09792). Another class of L-type calcium channel blockers includes 1,3-diphosphonates, such as verfosodyl.
[0022]
Accordingly, the present invention also relates to the use of α-LTX binding transmembrane receptors to identify novel calcium channel blockers. Seven-fold helical transmembrane receptors are particularly preferred for use for this purpose, and are particularly preferred G-protein coupled receptors. The use of transmembrane receptors of the secretin family is particularly highly preferred. Most preferred is the use of the HC110-R receptor set forth in SEQ ID NO: 2 and receptor proteins that are 70%, preferably 80%, particularly preferably 90%, and very preferably 95% homologous thereto. is there.
[0023]
The available data further indicate that HC110-R is a target for the novel anthelmintic depsipeptide BAY44-4400. BAY44-4400 blocks signaling by α-LTX in HEK-293 cells transfected with HC110-R (FIG. 12). This interference can result from the ionotropic activity of BAY44-4400, as is typical for other depsipeptides, such as beauvericin, enniatin, and the like (Geβner et al., 1996). However, BAY44-4400 does not cause any changes in untransfected cells. Furthermore, BAY44-4400 is a mouse β2Does not interfere with isoproterenol-induced signal transduction through HEK-293 cells transfected with adrenergic receptors. In addition, BAY44-4400 acts as an antagonist of α-LTX, but alone by Ca in HEK-293 cells transfected with HC110-R.2+Does not affect concentration.
[0024]
HC110-R protein
The membrane protein described in DE 197 04 024 A1 has been identified as a potential target protein for the anthelmintic active PF1022A. A λZAPII cDNA expression library of the parasitic nematode Haemonchus contortus was prepared and screened using a conjugate of PF1022A with KLH (keyhole limpet hemocyanin) PF1022A-KLH and a polyclonal antibody against this conjugate. A potential target protein was identified (see Example 1). Non-propagating recombinant clone about 1.5 × 106According to the test of H. A 3036 bp cDNA clone was found that hybridized with the 3.6 kb mRNA from S. contortus (see also Example 2). Using the RACE PCR method, the 3 'end and the 5' end were complemented (Example 4). Finally, a cDNA having a length of 3539 bp was obtained and designated as HC110-R. This cDNA is ATG100Encodes 986 amino acids (110 kDa) with an open reading frame starting with (Figure 2). This initiation codon is surrounded by Kozak sequences for optimal initiation of translation. The derived molecular weight of this protein was confirmed by in vitro translation of HC110-R RNA transcribed in vitro.
[0025]
The amino acid sequence of the HC110-R protein shows some specific structures. The extracellular N-terminal portion of this protein consists of a total of 535 residues. The N-terminus contains a 21 amino acid long signal peptide and a cleavage site at position 18. Next, there is a so-called "Thr stretch" (AA 128-147) in which the lectin-like sequence (AA 22-215) and the serine at position 144 are only interrupted. Downstream of this "Thr stretch" is the structure CX9WX12CX9WXCX5WX9CX3There is a cysteine-rich (rich) motif with W (AA166-221). In addition, the HC110-R protein contains a hydrophobic helical transmembrane domain seven times between 536 and 772 residues. Immediately upstream of this transmembrane region, the structure CXWWX6WX4CX11There is also a 4-Cys region of CXC (AA 478-524). In the transmembrane region there are three extracellular loops containing residues 587-597, 654-673 and 743-749, and three intracellular loops (positions 559-569, 627-636, 696-724). . The C-terminus is 214 residues (24 kDa) in length and includes a proline-rich portion (AA845-861) and a PEST region (AA915-933). Finally, there are three additional putative N-glycosylation sites at residues 26, 499 and 862, and 14 putative phosphorylation sites in the derived intracellular domain (see also FIG. 6). ).
[0026]
According to database analysis, the HC110-R protein was found to be genomic clone B0457 (Genebank) of the nematode Caenorhabditis elegans.TMAccession number Z54306) was found to be 48% identical and 78% similar to the unknown transmembrane protein (10014 AA) (see also FIG. 3).
[0027]
As used herein, the term "identity" refers to the number of sequence sites that match in a so-called alignment. This is shown as a percentage of the alignment length.
[0028]
The term "similarity" as used herein is the similarity of sequences based on a similarity measure, in other words, a measure of how similar they are, for example, assuming valine as threonine or leucine. .
[0029]
As used herein, the term "homologous" means an evolutionary relationship, in other words, whether two homologous proteins are derived from a common ancestral sequence. The term need not usually be related to identity or similarity apart from the fact that homologous sequences are usually more similar or have more matches in alignments than non-homologous sequences.
[0030]
Comparison of the two sequences reveals features common to both proteins, such as, for example, lectin-like sequences, “Thr stretch”, Cys motifs and PEST sequences. The highest identity is found in the transmembrane region (62%), whereas the identity in the N-terminal region (44%) and the C-terminal region (50%) is less pronounced.
[0031]
In addition, the HC110-R protein has 20-30% identity to the 7-fold helical G protein-coupled transmembrane receptor (GPCR), particularly the secretin subfamily. Comparison of the seven transmembrane domains shows high identity and similarity between the various GPCRs of the secretin subfamily and HC110-R in structure and sequence (FIG. 4).
[0032]
Latrophilin, a member of the secretin subfamily, derived from mammals such as humans (GenebankTMAccession number: E1360690), bovine (eg, G416021, G416053 and G4185804), and rat-derived (U78105 or U72487) show somewhat higher identity to HC110-R than other secretin receptors. . In particular, the identity of the transmembrane regions is between 45 and 48%. The HC110-R and the 1466 amino acid rat latrophilin-1 GPCR (U78105) exhibit common features, such as, for example, a lectin domain, a cysteine-rich domain, and a conserved 4-Cys motif in front of the transmembrane region. The latter has recently been shown to be a proteolytic site for latrophilin and other large secretin GPCRs. By comparison, the N-terminus of HC110-R does not include the olfactomedin and Pro / Thr regions of latrophylline, but latrophilin instead has no "Thr stretch" of HC110-R.
[0033]
Accordingly, the present application further relates to the use of a G protein-coupled transmembrane receptor with a seven transmembrane domain from a helminth to identify substances with anthelmintic activity. According to the invention, the use of transmembrane receptors which the secretin subfamily may have is preferred.
[0034]
Localization in cells
Transient transfection experiments were performed in various mammalian cell lines, such as COS-7 cells or HEK-293 cells, using the HC110-R-GFP fusion protein (FIG. 7). H. Heterologous expression was chosen because the controlus cell line has not yet been established.
[0035]
Green fluorescent protein (GFP) from the Pacific jellyfish Aequorea victoria can be used to localize proteins in living cells (see FIG. 8). GFP is used at the cellular level as an in vivo reporter to indicate the frequency of transient or stable transfections, and at the subcellular level to determine protein localization. Wild-type GFP is a 27 kDa monomer composed of 238 amino acids that emits green light up to 509 nm after excitation by UV light (360-400 nm; 395 nm max) or blue light (440-480 nm; 475 nm max). No substance or cofactor is required (Chalphi et al., $ 1994). Thus, GFP can be directly detected in vivo by fluorescence microscopy and its fluorescence characteristics remain essentially unchanged even if it is part of the fusion protein. EGFP (enhanced GFP) is a genetic variant of wild-type GFP and is used for transfecting mammalian cells (Yang et al., 1996). The maximum excitation of EGFP is65Was moved to the only 490 nm peak by replacing with Thr. Vectors pEGFP-C1 (Genebank Accession Number: U55763) and pEGFP-N3 (Genebank Accession Number: U55762) [Clontech, Palo Alto, CA, U.S.A. S. A. ] Can be used to express EGFP under the eradication of a strong constitutive CMV promoter and to fuse another protein to each of the N- and C-termini of EGFP.
[0036]
Stable cell lines are advantageous over transient expression in that all cells constitutively express the desired protein and can isolate the desired protein after localization. Select an expression vector that requires an antibody against the desired protein to detect the protein with the aid of fluorescence microscopy or Western blot, or that fuses the Myc or His tag to the C-terminus of the actual protein in the correct reading frame It is appropriate to do so, and in most cases, even if it is a monoclonal antibody, an antibody against it can be purchased.

Effect of α-Latrotoxin on HC110-R protein
To further demonstrate the similarity between HC110-R and latrophilin, and to test the function of recombinantly expressed HC110-R, HEK-293 cells were purified using the HC110-R-GFP fusion protein. Transfected and stably transfected transiently and stimulated with α-Latrotoxin (α-LTR).
[0039]
α-Latrotoxin is a presynaptic neurotoxin that can be isolated from the venom of the Latrodectus mactans. Its toxicity to the vertebrate central nervous system is known;2+]iCauses neuronal depolarization by stimulating non-eliminating exocytosis of neurotransmitters. Thus, it was also clarified that the effect of α-latrotoxin was mediated, at least in part, by latrophilin. Furthermore, the toxicity of α-Latrotoxin is presumed to be due to its ability to interact with receptors (GPCRs) that couple to GTP binding proteins. These receptors usually mediate the effects of endogenous hormones or neuropeptides (Holz and Habener 1998).
[0040]

[0058]
The term "polypeptide" as used herein refers to both short amino acid chains, commonly referred to as peptides, oligopeptides or oligomers, and long amino acid chains, commonly referred to as proteins. This includes amino acid chains that can be modified either by natural processes, such as by post-translational processing, or by state-of-the-art chemical methods. Such modifications can occur at various sites in the polypeptide, and one or more may occur, for example, in the peptide backbone, at the amino acid side chains, at the amino-terminal host carboxy-terminus. These include, for example, acetylation, acylation, ADP ribosylation, amidation, flavin, heme moieties, nucleotides or nucleotide derivatives, lipids or lipid derivatives or covalent bonds with phosphatidylinositol, cyclization, disulfide bridge formation, dimethylation, Cystine formation, formylation, gamma-carboxylation, glycosylation, hydroxylation, iodination, methylation, myristoylation, oxidation, proteolytic processing, phosphorylation, selenoylation and tRNA-mediated amino acid addition are included.
[0059]
Polypeptides can be used according to the invention in the form of a "mature" protein or as part of a larger protein (eg, a fusion protein). This may further include secretory or “leader” sequences, pro-sequences, sequences that allow for easy purification (eg, multiple histidine residues), or additional stabilizing amino acids.
[0060]
The homologous protein or polypeptide is at least 70%, preferably 80%, particularly preferably at least 70% with the sequence shown in SEQ ID NO: 2 described in the document DE-A-197 04 024 (the teachings of this document are included in the present application). Is 90%, very particularly preferably 95% identical, a protein or polypeptide having at least 20, preferably at least 25, particularly preferably at least 30 contiguous amino acids, very particularly preferably its full length. .
[0061]
According to the use of the polypeptides of the present invention, the polypeptide need not represent the entire receptor, but may only be a fragment thereof, as long as it has at least the biological activity of the entire receptor. In addition, the polypeptide is H. It does not need to be derived from the transmembrane receptor. A polypeptide corresponding to a helminth or even a transmembrane receptor of another species of arthropod or a fragment thereof as long as it can exert the biological activity of that receptor is according to the invention.
[0062]
With respect to the use of the polypeptides of the present invention, the polypeptide may be deleted or deleted as compared to the corresponding region of the native GPC receptor, as long as it exerts at least one biological activity of the entire GPC receptor. It may have amino acid substitutions. Conservative substitutions are preferred. Such conservative substitutions include variants in which one amino acid has been replaced with another amino acid from the following group:
1. Small aliphatic, non-polar or slightly polar residues: Ala, Ser, Thr, Pro and Gly;
2. Polar, negatively charged residues and their amides: Asp, Asn, Glu and Gln;
3. Polar, positively charged residues: His, Arg and Lys;
4. Large aliphatic, non-polar residues: Met, Leu, Ile, Val and Cys;
5. Aromatic residues: Phe, Tyr and Trp.

As used herein, the term “hybridize” refers to the process by which a single-stranded nucleic acid molecule base pairs with a complementary strand. Starting from the sequence of information described herein, for example, DNA fragments encoding polypeptides having GPC receptor biological activity from other nematodes other than C. contortus and from arthropods can be isolated.
[0067]
For suitable probes, the amino and carboxy terminal cDNA portions are preferred. Hybridization conditions are chosen such that low similarity sequences from other organisms can also be detected. Hybridization conditions with low stringency may be as follows: For example, hybridization is performed at 40-55 ° C. in 6 × SSC / 0% formamide as a hybridization solution. The conditions of the second washing step must be tested, for example, first at 50 ° C. in 2 × SSC, and then assess the intensity of the signal. Next, the washing conditions are changed.
[0068]
Suitable hybridization conditions are shown below by way of example:
Hybridization solution: 6 × SSC / 0% formamide, preferred hybridization solution: 6 × SSC / 0% formamide
Hybridization temperature: 34 ° C, preferred hybridization temperature: 42 ° C
First washing step: 2 × SSC at 40 ° C.
Second washing step: 2 × SSC at 45 ° C .; Preferred second washing step: 0.6 × SSC at 55 ° C .: Particularly preferred second washing step: 0.3 × SSC at 65 ° C.
[0069]
Hybridization conditions are calculated as appropriate according to the following formula:
Melting temperature Tm = 81.5 ° C. + 16.6 log [c (Na+)] + 0.41 (% G + C))-500 / n
(Lottspeich and Zorbas @ 1998).
[0070]
Where c is the concentration and n is the length of the base-pair hybridizing sequence portion. The 500 / n term is excluded for sequences greater than 100 bp. The highest stringency wash is at an ionic strength of 15 mM Na + (equivalent to 0.1 × SSC) at a temperature 5-15 ° C. below the Tm. When an RNA probe is used for hybridization, the dissolution temperature increases by 10 to 15 ° C.

Furthermore, the present invention relates to a method for producing a polypeptide used according to the present invention. A polypeptide encoded by a known nucleic acid can be produced by culturing a host cell containing the nucleic acid under preferable conditions. The desired polypeptide can then be isolated from the cells or medium by conventional methods. The polypeptide can also be produced in an in vitro system.
[0099]
A rapid method for isolating a polypeptide according to the invention synthesized by a host cell using a nucleic acid according to the invention is to affinity purify the fusion partner in a simple manner, for example as described in the examples. Initiated by expression of the possible fusion protein. Fusion partners include, for example, glutathione S-transferase. The fusion protein can then be purified on a glutathione affinity column. The fusion partner can be removed by partial proteolytic cleavage, for example, with a linker between the fusion partner and the polypeptide of the invention to be purified. The linker can be designed to include a target amino acid such as an arginine or lysine residue that defines a site for cleavage by trypsin. Such linkers can be made by using standard cloning techniques using oligonucleotides. Another possible method is to use a histidine fusion protein and use Ni2+Based on its purification on Talon columns.
[0100]
Further possible purification methods include preparative electrophoresis, FPLC, HPLC (e.g. using a gel filtration column, reversed phase column or a lightly hydrophobic column), gel filtration, differential purification. , Ion exchange chromatography and affinity chromatography.
[0101]
Since receptor-like protein kinases are membrane proteins, in this purification method, for example, detergents that have little or no effect on the secondary and tertiary structure of the polypeptide, such as nonionic surfactants Preferably, surfactant extraction is performed using a surfactant.

[0103]
As used herein, the term "isolated or purified" refers to separating a polypeptide from other proteins or other macromolecules of cells or tissues. Preferably, a composition of the invention comprising a polypeptide is at least 10-fold, particularly preferably at least 100-fold, enriched in protein compared to preparations derived from host cells.
[0104]
Further, the polypeptide of the present invention can be affinity-purified without using a fusion partner by using an antibody that binds to the polypeptide.
[0105]
Furthermore, the present invention relates to an antibody that specifically binds to the above polypeptide or receptor. Such antibodies are purified by conventional methods. For example, such antibodies have been used in H.sub. The transmembrane receptor of the present invention, such as the HC110-R receptor from S. contortus, or a fragment thereof, may be produced by injecting an amount sufficient for antibody production and then isolating the antibody. Furthermore, immortalized cell lines which produce monoclonal antibodies can be obtained in a manner known per se. Antibodies can be appropriately labeled using a detection reagent. Preferred examples of such labeling reagents include enzymes, radiolabeled elements, fluorescent chemicals, or biotin. Instead of a complete antibody, it is also possible to use fragments having the desired specific binding properties.
[0106]
As used herein, the term “agonist” refers to a molecule that activates a transmembrane receptor.
[0107]
As used herein, the term "antagonist" refers to a molecule that displaces or inhibits the function of an agonist at the binding site of the agonist.
[0108]
The term "modulator" as used herein is a generic term for agonists and antagonists. A modulator may be a small organic compound molecule, peptide or antibody that binds a polypeptide according to the invention. Further, a modulator may be a small organic compound molecule, peptide or antibody that binds to a molecule, which in turn affects its biological activity by binding to a polypeptide of the invention. . Modulators can be mimics of natural substrates and ligands.
[0109]
Preferably, the modulator is a small organic compound.
[0110]
Binding of modulators to the polypeptides can alter the processes of helminth or arthropod cells treated with them, resulting in death.
[0111]
Thus, the invention further extends to the use of polypeptide modulators as anthelmintics and arthropodicides.
[0112]
The invention likewise relates in particular to the use of α-LTX as an anthelmintic.
[0113]
Also, the use according to the invention of a nucleic acid or polypeptide in the method of the invention makes it possible to find compounds which bind to the receptor of the invention. Similarly, the latter can be used as an anthelmintic, for example as a nematicide for plants or as an anthelmintic active for animals. For example, a host cell containing a nucleic acid and expressing its corresponding receptor or polypeptide, or its gene product, can be treated under conditions that allow the host cell, receptor or individual polypeptide to interact with at least one compound. Contact with a compound or mixture of compounds.
[0114]
The invention relates to transmembrane receptors from helminths or arthropods, preferably GPCRs of the secretin subfamily, particularly preferably H. a nematicidal active substance that binds to a receptor HC110-R from C. contortus and binds to a receptor whose sequence matches 70%, preferably 80%, particularly preferably 90% and even more preferably 95% of them. Particularly relevant are methods suitable for identification. However, the method may be practiced with HC110-R homologous receptors from species other than those described herein. The method of using the receptor other than HC110-R of the present invention is completely included in the present invention.
[0115]
The methods according to the present invention include high-throughput screening (eg, high-throughput screening (HTS) and ultra-high-throughput screening (UHTS)). For this purpose, both host cells and cell-free preparations containing the nucleic acids of the invention and / or the polypeptides of the invention can be used.
[0116]
Cell-free test system
Many test systems aimed at testing compounds and natural extracts are designed for high throughput in order to maximize the number of substances tested in a given time period. Test systems based on cell-free operation require purified or semi-purified proteins. They are suitable for "early" tests, which are mainly aimed at detecting the potential effect of a substance on the target protein.
[0117]
Effects such as cytotoxicity are usually neglected in these in vitro systems. This test system further tests both the inhibitory or inhibitory and stimulatory effects of the substance. The effect of a substance can be confirmed by a series of concentration-dependent tests. A control mixture without test substance can be used to evaluate its effect.
[0118]
Cell-based test system
The development of a cell-based test system for identifying substances that modulate the activity of HC110-R and homologous receptors has been developed with cell lines stably transfected with the HC110-R receptor that can be used according to the present invention. Although possible, they can also be developed with corresponding homologous receptors from other species that can be identified according to the present invention.
[0119]
Similarly, the present invention allows for the identification of other compounds that are effective as calcium channel blockers.
[0120]
Modulators can be used to modulate a synthesis reaction mixture (eg, the product of in vitro translation) or a material that constitutes a cell, eg, a membrane or any other preparation containing the polypeptide, in the presence of candidate molecules that can be agonists and antagonists, or It can be found by incubating with a labeled substrate or ligand of the polypeptide in the absence. The ability of a candidate molecule to increase or decrease the activity of a polypeptide of the invention will be evident from increasing or decreasing the binding of a labeled ligand or increasing or decreasing the conversion of a labeled substrate. Molecules that bind well and increase the activity of the polypeptide of the invention are agonists. Molecules that bind well but do not cause the biological activity of the polypeptide according to the invention are probably good antagonists.
[0121]
Scintillation proximity assay (SPA)
One possibility for identifying substances that modulate the activity of HC110-R and its homologous receptor proteins is called a scintillation proximity assay (SPA) (EP-A-015 473). This test system utilizes the interaction of a radiolabeled ligand (eg, a small organic molecule or a second radiolabeled protein molecule) with a receptor (eg, HC110-R). In this case, the receptor is bound to microparticles or beads provided with the scintillating molecule. During the decay of radioactivity, the spherical scintillating material is excited by the elementary particles of the radioactive marker and emits detectable photons. The test conditions are optimized such that only particles emitted by the ligand to emit a signal will be emitted by the ligand bound to the receptor or HC110-R.
[0122]
In one possible embodiment, HC110-R is bound to beads with or without interaction or binding with a test substance. Furthermore, in this case, a fragment of the HC110-R receptor could also be used. The radiolabeled ligand can be, for example, labeled α-LTX, nifedipine or labeled depsipeptide. When the binding ligand binds to the immobilized HC110-R receptor, the ligand is present between the immobilized HC110-R and the labeled ligand to bind itself to the area of the contact moiety. Will need to be inhibited or destroyed. Successful binding to the labeled HC110-R receptor can then be detected by flash. Similarly, the complex between the immobilized labeled ligand and the non-immobilized labeled ligand is destroyed by the binding of the test substance and attenuates to an intensity that can be detected by a flash. The test system then responds to the auxiliary inhibition system
[0123]
Two hybrid system
Another example of a whole cell based test system is what is called a two-hybrid system. A specific example is a so-called interaction trap. This involves the genetic selection of interacting proteins in yeast (see, eg, Gyuris et al., 1993). The test system is designed to detect and delineate the interaction of the two proteins through successful interactions that produce a detectable signal.
[0124]
Such a test system can be applied to test a large amount of a test substance within a predetermined period.
[0125]
This system is based on the construction of two vectors, a "decoy" vector and a "prey" vector. The gene encoding the HC110-R of the present invention or a fragment thereof is cloned into a decoy vector, and then expressed as a fusion protein with a LexA protein which is a DNA binding protein. A second gene encoding an HC110-R interaction partner, eg, α-LTX, is cloned into a bait vector and expressed as a fusion protein with the B42 bait protein. Both vectors are present in Saccharomyces cerevisiae hosts that contain a copy of LexA-binding DNA 5 'to the lacZ or HIS2 reporter gene. Interaction between the two fusion proteins activates transcription of the receptor gene. If the interaction is inhibited or disrupted by the presence of the test substance, the two fusion proteins can no longer interact and no reporter gene product is produced.
[0126]
Replacement test
An example of another way in which modulators of the polypeptides according to the invention can be found are displacement tests, which, under conditions suitable for this purpose, comprise a potential modulator of the polypeptides of the invention and potential modulators. Is a test in which a compound known to bind to the polypeptide of the present invention, for example, a natural substrate or ligand, or a substrate or ligand mimic is combined. α-LTX is preferably used in this test according to the method of the present invention.
[0127]
Known analytical systems, such as those of Biacore AB, Uppsala, Sweden, are based on the complete HC110-R protein, or the N-host C-terminal deletion mutant of HC110-R, in vitro mutagenesis or other known methods. Other variants of the modified HC110-R molecule can be used for molecular interaction studies. This includes one
(I) Binding of the HC110-R receptor or a fragment thereof by known chemical methods (coupling via amines, thiols, aldehydes), or affinity binding to a biochip (eg, streptavidin-biotin, IMAC) or, to another,
(Ii) It is necessary to attach α-LTX or another modulator, such as BAY44-4400 or another potential ligand, to the chip as described in (i).
[0128]
The binding between the immobilized molecule and a ligand (such as the HC110-R protein or any modulator, such as BAY44-4400) present in solution is physically measured. The ligand is immobilized on a Biacore Instrument on a sensor chip having a thin layer of gold. The analyte solution is diffused by the micro flow cell on the chip. Binding of the analyte to the immobilized ligand increases the local concentration of the surface and gradually increases the refractive index of the gold layer near the medium. This is an effect on the interaction between free electrons (plasmons) in the metal and photons emitted from the instrument. This physical change is proportional to the mass and number of molecules on the chip, and its ligand-analyte binding can be recorded in real-time and the apparent binding / dissociation constant determined (Fivash et al., 1998). The specificity of the binding is demonstrated by competition experiments.
[0129]
In addition, the corresponding measurements are used to determine the HC110-R protein domain important for ligand binding and to identify new, previously undisclosed ligands for HC110-R.
[0130]
Calcium imaging
Calcium imaging or signaling is considered as another method of detecting substances that interact with HC110-R (see, for example, FIGS. 11 and 10). This requires the use of calcium indicators to help detect changes in intracellular calcium levels. HC110-R expressing cells loaded with a calcium indicator are used in this method. When there is calcium influx caused by the HC110-R agonist, or release of intracellular calcium, there is a change in absorbance under UV irradiation as a function of the calcium uptake of the indicator. Antagonists can be identified in this system by completely or partially inhibiting the calcium signal induced by an agonist (eg, α-LTX). Possible calcium indicators preferred for this purpose include Fura-2 (Sigma) or Indo-1 (molecular probes).
[0131]
In addition, calcium indicators are excited by visible light and their fluorescent properties change in a detectable manner depending on calcium uptake. Indicators Fluo-3 and Fluo-4 have high calcium affinity. Fluo-4 has a strong fluorescent signal and is particularly preferred for measurement in test systems that use cells only at low concentrations, as in the case of HEK-293 cells. Further, as indicators, Rhod-2, x-Rhod-1, Fluo-5N, Fluo-5F, Mag-Fluo-4, Rhod-5F, Rhod-5N, Y-Rhod-5N, Mag-Rhod-2, Mag -X-Rhod-1, calcium green-1 and -2, calcium green-5N, Oregon green 488 BAPTA-1, Oregon green 488 BAPTA-2 and -5N, Fura red, calcein and the like.
[0132]
Another method of loading a calcium indicator into cells is recombinant expression of a photoprotein in target cells. These photoproteins respond to emit light when they form a complex with calcium ions. Aequorin is a photoprotein that is already widely used in many research and test systems. Cells that express the target protein simultaneously with aequorin are first loaded with the luminophore coelenterazine in this test method. Apoaequorin formed by cells forms a complex with coelenterazine and carbon dioxide. Subsequently, calcium also enters the cells and, when bound to this complex, releases carbon dioxide and emits blue light (maximum emission about 466 nm). The light emission in this case correlates with the concentration of calcium present in the cell.
[0133]
Thus, the invention also relates to the use of HC110-R, fragments thereof, or similar proteins from other organisms, wherein the function of the receptor or the binding of a modulator to the receptor is aequorin or a similar photoprotein. Detected by a light signal mediated by
[0134]

[0160]
Example
1. Construction and screening of cDNA library
Construction of a cDNA library, production of a KLH-PF1022A conjugate, and antiserum against PF1022A, and immunoscreening of a cDNA library and DNA analysis were performed as described in WO 98/15625.
[0161]
2. RNA isolation
Total RNA was isolated by extraction from adult Haemonchus contortus nematodes by GTC / CsCl cushion method (Sambrook et al., 1989) or obtained in one step by GTC / phenol / chloroform extraction (Chomczynski and Sacchi 1987). . Poly (A)+RNA was isolated by chromatography on oligo (dT) cellulose (Aviv and Leder, 1972).
[0162]
3. Northern blotting
Gluoxylated total RNA (20 μg per lane) derived from Haemonchus contortus was fractionated on an agarose gel (Sambrook et al., 1989; McMaster and Carmichael 1977), and standard capillary transport method (the basic capsular transport chemistry, medium and free shipping). To move to a Hybond N membrane (Amersham). The radiolabeled probe was purchased from Megaprime Kit (Amersham, Braunschweig, Germany) and 50 μCi of [α-32P] dCTP (3000 Ci / mmol, ICN, Meckenheim, Germany) was prepared by random labeling of the linearized plasmid DNA (HC110-R). Hybridization was performed using 6 × SSC (1 × SSC: 0.15 M NaCl, 0.015 M sodium citrate), 5 × Denhardt's reagent (0.1% polyvinylpyrrolidone, 0.1% BSA, 0.1% Ficoll) 400), 0.1% SDS and 100 μg / mL herring sperm DNA at 65 ° C. overnight. The filters were washed and exposed at 65 ° C. with high stringency in 0.1 × SSC and 0.1% SDS (−80 ° C. Kodak BioMax MS film) (see FIG. 1 (A)).
[0163]
4.5 'and 3' RACE PCR
Using the 5 '/ 3' RACE method, the missing 5 'and 3' ends of the identified cDNA clones were isolated.
[0164]
5 'RACE is based on specifically amplifying the 5' end of mRNA-derived genes. First strand cDNA is synthesized using sequence specific primers and AMV reverse transcriptase. Attachment of the poly (A) tail to the product allows the use of oligo dT anchor primers and nested sequence specific primers in subsequent PCR. In another PCR, another nested primer can be used to ensure specificity.
[0165]
In 3 'RACE, the first cDNA strand is synthesized using an oligo dT primer, and subsequent PCR reactions are performed using sequence-specific primers.
[0166]
The cDNA was purified using primers 5'-GGT CAC CGT CGT CCC AGA AA-3 'and 1 g H.C. using the 5' RACE kit from GIBCO BRL (Eggenstein, Germany). contortus synthesized from total RNA. Supercrypt reverse transcriptase was used for this purpose. C tailing of the C-terminus of this cDNA was performed using terminal deoxynucleotidyl transferase. The first amplification consisted of a 400 nM oligodeoxyinosyl anchor primer (5′-CUA CUA CUA CUA GGC CAC GCG TCG ACT AGT ACG GGI IGG GII GGG IIG-3 ′) and a 400 nM first nested primer 5′-. Using CCA TTC GAT TCC TCT TCT CG-3 ′ (Birsner and Grob, Denzlingen, Germany), 200 μM of each dNTP and 1.5 mM of MgCl 2 were used.2Performed in 50 μl containing 1/5 tail cDNA and 2.5 U of native Taq polymerase. The first denaturation was performed at 94 ° C. for 5 minutes, then 35 cycles of 94 ° C. for 1 minute, 53 ° C. for 1 minute and 72 ° C. for 10 minutes, followed by a final synthesis step at 72 ° C. for 10 minutes. The reaction conditions for the nested PCR were as follows: 1 μl of the first amplification product was used as a template, the gene-specific second nested primer 5′-GTC GAT GGT GCA GAT TTC GC-3 ′, anchor primer (5′-CUA CUA CUA) CUA GGC CAC GCG TCG ACT AGT AC-3 ′) is the same as described above, except that the cycle was performed with only 25 cycles at an annealing temperature of 53 ° C.
[0167]
3 'RACE PCR (GIBCO BRL, Eggenstein, Germany) was used for adult H. starting from preincubation at 70 ° C. for 10 minutes with 1 μg of total RNA from S. contortus and 500 nM of oligo dT adapter primer 5′-GGC CAC GCG TCG ACT AGT ACT TTT TTT TTT TTT TTT TTT T-3 ′; C. for 2 minutes. 2.5 mM MgCl in 20 μl2After the addition of 500 μM, 10 μM DTT of each dNTP and 200 U of Super-Script II reverse transcriptase, the cDNA was incubated at 42 ° C. for 50 minutes and in the last step at 70 ° C. for 15 minutes and 4 ° C. for 10 minutes. E. FIG. RNA was removed by incubating at 37 ° C. for 10 minutes using E. coli RNase H 2U. The first denaturation step is performed at 94 ° C. for 3 minutes, then 35 cycles of 94 ° C. for 1 minute, 51 ° C. for 1 minute and 72 ° C. for 2 minutes, and the final synthesis step is carried out at 72 ° C. For 15 minutes. Unless otherwise stated, 2 μl of the first amplification was used for nested PCR and the other conditions were the same, but in this case the short adapter primer 5′-GGC CAC GCG TCG ACT AGT AC-3 ′ and the nested primer 30 cycles were performed using 5'-ACA CTC TAA TCT CCA ACT G-3 '. The PCR product was analyzed on a 2% agarose gel, eluted and cloned into the TA vector pMosBlue (Amersham, Braunschweig, Germany).
[0168]
5. RNA transfer
Transfer of fractionated RNA from glyoxal gel to neutral Hybond N nylon membrane [Amersham, Braunschweig] and transfer of genomic DNA from TBE agarose gel were carried out in the alkaline transfer solution by the Chomczynski method (1992). Perform for 2 hours by downward alkaline capillary transport. The membrane was then neutralized in a 0.2 M sodium phosphate buffer (pH 6.8) for 20 minutes, dried at 80 ° C. for 20-60 minutes and baked. To hybridize with the radiolabeled probe, place the membrane in a plastic bag at 5 ml / cm2 And incubated at 65 ° C for 3 hours. The buffer is changed to a hybridization solution for hybridization. Rapid Hyb. If a solution [Amersham, Braunschweig] is used, prehybridization occurs at 65 ° C. for 30 minutes without additional prehybridization solution. After the addition of a probe radiolabeled by random priming, hybridization is carried out at 65 ° C. overnight. Thereafter, the membrane is washed once at 65 ° C. for 20 minutes using 2 × SSC / 0.1% SDS and three times for 1 hour each using 0.1 × SSC / 0.1% SDS. did. The membrane is exposed to Kodak X-OMAT or Kodak BIOMAX-MS X-ray film at -80 ° C using a suitable intensifying screen.
[0169]
6. In vivo transcription and translation
The TNT T7 / T3 coupled reticulocyte lysate system (Promega) was used according to the manufacturer's protocol,35The entire coding sequence of HC110-R was transcribed and translated in the presence of S-labeled methionine and cysteine (ICN, Eschwege, Germany). 40 μCi35S-labeled mixture (> 1000 Ci / mmol, ICN, Meckenheim, Germany), rabbit reticulocyte lysate system (Promega, Serva, Heidelberg) using 1 μg of circularized HC110-R plasmid DNA and 10 U of T3 RNA polymerase. Was used to translate the RNA. The reaction was performed at 30 ° C. for 90 minutes. The positive control contained 1 μg of luciferase control DNA.
[0170]
The reaction products were fractionated by SDS polyacrylamide gel electrophoresis (Laemmli 1970) and analyzed fluorometrically using an amplified fluorography solution (Amersham Pharmacia Biotech) or 1 M sodium salicylate (pH 7) (Chamberlain 1979) and The gel was dried and exposed (Kodak BioMax MR film at -8O <0> C with sensitizer) (see Figure 1 (B)).
[0171]
Alternatively, the MAXIscript in vitro transcription kit from Ambion (Heidelberg) was used for the in vitro synthesis of RNA transcripts from HC110-R cDNA cloned into pBluescript SK. 4 μg of HC110-R plasmid DNA was linearized with the restriction enzyme Hind III or Sal I after the stop codon, extracted with phenol / chloroform, precipitated with 3 volumes of ethanol and DEPC / H2Dissolved in O. 2 μg of HC110-R cDNA in 50 μl of the reaction mixture was combined with 2.5 μl of 200 mM DTT, 2.5 μl each of 10 mM ATP, CTP, GTP and UTP, 5 μl of 10 × transcription buffer, RNasin inhibitor (40 U / μl) (Promega, Heidelberg) 1 0.6 μl and 2 μl of T3 phage polymerase (10 U / μl) and incubated at 37 ° C. for 2 hours. One hour later, 2 μl of T3 phage polymerase (10 U / μl) was further added. This mixture is mixed with 1.5 μl of RNase-free DNase I (2 U / μl) and 1 μl of RNasin inhibitor (40 U / μl), incubated at 37 ° C. for 15 minutes, extracted with phenol / chloroform and tripled Precipitated in an amount of ethanol, DEPC / H2Resuspended in 25 μl O. One fifth of the volume of the sample was analyzed on a glyoxal gel.
[0172]
7. DNA analysis
Clones were sequenced by dideoxynucleotide chain termination with the aid of automated laser fluorescence sequence analysis (LICOR 4000; MWG, Ebersberg, Germany) and Thermo Sequenase fluorescent labeling cycle sequencing kit (Amersham, Braunschweig, Germany). The sequences of both strands were determined, and the sequence data was analyzed with GCG software (Genetics Computer Group Inc., Madison, WI, USA) and PC / GENE software (Intelligenetics, Mountain View, CA, USA). Using the programs FASTA (Pearson and Lipman 1988), BLITZ (Smith and Waterman 1981), and BLAST (Altschul and Lipmann 1990), the EMBL and Swiss plot protein databases (Swiss-Prot protein) for the sequence similarity of the resulting protein sequences. databases). Protein sequences were analyzed using SAPS (Brendel et al., 1992) and PROSITE and Prot-Param (Appel et al., 1994).
[0173]
8. Preparation of protein extract from Haemonchus controlus
H.Frozen in liquid nitrogen 50-100 mg of controlus were added to 1 ml of TRIZOL [Gibco, Karlsruhe]. The nematodes were homogenized with TRIZOL in a glass container for 3 × 15 seconds and incubated at room temperature for 5 minutes. After adding 200 μl of chloroform per ml of TRIZOL, the sample was stirred for 15 seconds, the mixture was incubated at room temperature for another 2-3 minutes, and centrifuged at 4 ° C. for 10 minutes at 7000-12000 rpm. The upper aqueous phase contains RNA, the intermediate phase contains genomic DNA, and the red organic phase contains proteins (Coombs et al., 1990; Chomczynski 1993). The aqueous phase was removed and treated separately. The interphase and organic phase were mixed with 300 μl of 100% ethanol per ml of TRIZOL, mixed well and incubated at room temperature for 2-3 minutes. After centrifugation at 2000 rpm for 5 minutes at 4 ° C., the protein supernatant was carefully transferred to an Eppendorf vessel and precipitated with 1 ml of isopropanol for 10 minutes at room temperature. Centrifugation is again performed at 4 ° C. for 10 minutes at 12000 rpm, the supernatant is discarded and the protein precipitate is mixed with 2 ml of a 0.3 M guanidine hydrochloride solution in 95% ethanol, stirred and stirred at room temperature for 20 minutes. Incubate and centrifuge 3 times at 7,500 rpm for 5 minutes at 4 ° C. The pellet was then dissolved in 2 ml of 100% ethanol, precipitated at room temperature for 20 minutes and pelleted at 4500C for 5 minutes at 7500 rpm. The pellet was briefly vacuum dried and resuspended in urea lysis buffer (8M). Insoluble material was removed by centrifugation at 10,000 rpm for 10 minutes at 4 ° C. and the supernatant was transferred to a new Eppendorf vessel, after which the protein concentration was determined and stored at −20 ° C. until further processing.
[0174]
9. Preparation of protein extract from yeast cells
Protein extracts were prepared from cultured yeast cells by inoculating a single yeast colony in 5 ml of YPAD medium and shaking at 30 ° C. until saturation (2 days). A portion (2 ml) of the cultured yeast was centrifuged (Heraeus Biofuge 15 R) at 3000 rpm for 2 minutes at 4 ° C.2Washed once with O, resuspended in 250 μl yeast lysis buffer, transferred to a small test tube, filled with glass beads (φ 0.5 mm) just below the liquid level and stirred for 5 minutes at maximum setting. Then 4 × RotiLoad buffer (Roth, Karlsruhe) was added and the mixture was incubated at 95 ° C. for 5 minutes. The disrupted cells were transferred to an Eppendorf vessel and cell debris was removed by centrifugation (Eppendorf Centrifuge 5415 C) at 14000 rpm for 5 minutes. A 20 μl portion of the sample prepared by this method was run on an SDS polyacrylamide gel.
[0175]
10. E. FIG. Preparation of protein extract from E. coli cells
The protein extract was centrifuged at 5000 rpm for 5 minutes at 4 ° C. in a Heraeus flow centrifuge from 5 ml of the overnight culture to give 1 × 107E. E. coli cells were prepared by pelleting, washing with 5 ml of PBS and centrifuging again. The pellet was then resuspended in 1 ml of TRIZOL (Gibco, Karlsruhe) for further processing.
[0176]
As an alternative, the PBS-washed cell pellet is resuspended in PBS and the cells are pulsed with several short ultrasonic pulses (Sonifier B-12, Branson Sonic Power Company, Danbury, USA), liquid nitrogen. And destroyed by lysozyme.
[0177]
For subsequent protein analysis, 4 × RotiLoad buffer (Roth, Karlsruhe) was added and run on an SDS polyacrylamide gel to analyze fractions. The total amount of protein passed per lane was 10 to 20 μg.
[0178]
11. Preparation of protein extract from cultured cells
Confluent cell culture dishes of 35 mm adherent cells or 5-10 cells in FCS containing medium6Individual non-adherent animal cells are either removed beforehand by trypsinization with a trypsin / EDTA solution or mechanically detached after cooling using a cell scraper, transferred to an Eppendorf vessel and pelleted at 13000 rpm for 10 seconds at room temperature. , Washed twice with PBS and centrifuged again. After lysing the cells in 1 ml of TRIZOL, the cells were lysed by shaking vigorously or by aspirating the cells several times into the needle of a disposable syringe and incubating at room temperature for 5 minutes. As an alternative, the cell pellet is resuspended in 1 ml of PBS or in urea lysis buffer (8M) and sonicated for a very short time (Sonifier B-12, Branson Sonic Power Company, Danbury, USA). A.). The amount of protein is then measured by the method of Bradford (1976) or Lowry et al. (1951).
[0179]
12. E. FIG. inducible protein expression in E. coli
A polyclonal antibody against the HC110-R protein was cloned into the expression vector pRSETB (Invitrogen, Leek, NL), resulting in three HC110-R fragments fused to the N-terminus with 6 × His satisfying the reading frame, ie, , Complete HC110-R cDNA, N-terminus without transmembrane domain, and C-terminus after the seventh transmembrane domain.
[0180]
The complete coding region of HC110-R was replaced with P84_ATG BamHI '5' primer 5'-CTG CCG GAT CCT CGG TTT AAT ACC AACATG AGG-3 'and P3121_TGA HindIII 3' primer 5'-GCA CTA AGC TTG ACT GAA GCG CAC AAC CTC G-3 ', and the N-terminal to the first transmembrane domain is P84_ATG BamHI 5' Primer (see above) and P1434_TGA HindIII 3 ′ primer 5′-GGC TCA AGC TTATCA Amplified using GAG AAC AAG CGA CAC GGC-3 'and C-terminal beginning after the seventh transmembrane domain was P2486_ATG BamHI 5' primer 5'-CTA TCG GAT CCC AACATG Amplification was performed using GCT GGC TCC CGT GAT ACC TCT AGG-3 'and P3121_TGA HindIII 3' primers (see above). The annealing temperature of all three plasmid PCRs was 56 ° C. for the first 5 cycles and 62 ° C. for the last 30 cycles. The PCR product was digested with BamHI and HindIII enzymes and ligated directly into a pRSET B expression vector that was also linearized with BamHI / HindIII.
[0181]
In the pREST B vector, expression is controlled by the viral promoter of bacteriophage T7. Therefore, cloning was performed using XL1-Blue E. coli without the T7 RNA polymerase gene. E. coli strains. Next, the recombinant plasmid further comprises a plasmid pACYC184 stabilized by chloramphenicol resistance, and the expression level of T7 lysozyme, a natural inhibitor of T7 RNA polymerase, is low in T7 polymerase-expressing BL21 (De3) pLysSp. Transformed into E. coli cells. Since these cells are under the control of the lacUV5 promoter, IPTG induction causes the expression of T7 RNA polymerase and consequently the fusion protein.
[0182]
A single colony carrying the HC110-R plasmid of interest is transferred from a fresh LB plate supplemented with 50 μg / mL ampicillin and 35 μg / mL chloramphenicol to 50 ml of LB medium under the same selection pressure, until stationary phase Shake at 280 rpm at 37 ° C. overnight. This overnight culture is placed on an OD600Is diluted to 0.3, and 100 ml of this culture is OD600Was further shaken at 280 rpm at 37 ° C. until the pH became 0.6 to 0.5.
[0183]
1 OD600Were harvested and uninduced cells were briefly centrifuged and lysed in 150 μl of 8M urea lysis buffer pH 8.0 and 50 μl of 4 × RotiLoad buffer [Roth, Karlsruhe]. The uninduced sample was denatured for 2 minutes and the genomic DNA was sonicated with a short ultrasonic pulse of Sonifier B-12 [Branson Sonic Power Company, Danbury, U.S.A. S. A. [0184]
Expression of the fusion protein was induced by adding 1 mM IPTG, and 100 ml of the culture was incubated at 37 ° C. for an additional 3-4 hours. After incubation, the induced cells were centrifuged (Heraeus fluorescence centrifuge) at 5000 rpm, 4 ° C. for 15 minutes, the pellet was washed in PBS, and then resuspended in 8 ml of 8M urea lysis buffer. Cells were disrupted by submersion in liquid nitrogen and thawed at 37 ° C. three times. After the first nitrogen treatment, 0.75 mg / ml lysozyme was added. After a final incubation in liquid nitrogen, incubation at 16 ° C. for 20 minutes was followed by a short ultrasonic pulse of 10 seconds each while cooling in an ice-water bath until the solution had a viscosity equivalent to water. After centrifugation at 13000 rpm at 4 ° C. for 10 minutes (Beckman J2-21; JS 13.1-Rotor), 150 μl of the induced sample was taken out, mixed with 50 μl of 4 × RotiLoad buffer (Roth), and mixed with SDS-PAGE. Then, specific HC110-R protein fragments were checked along with uninduced samples by Coomassie staining or Western blot analysis using a mouse anti-His antibody.
[0185]
The remaining supernatant was transferred to a new container and stored at -20 ° C for further purification by affinity chromatography.

13. Protein purification by metal affinity chromatography
Concentration is performed under denaturing conditions under the conditions of Clontech [Palo Alto, U.S.A. S. A. ] TALON spin column with IMAC system ("ImmobilizedMetalAfinityCChromatography ") with an N-terminal 6 × His tag. First, the resin in the column was separately equilibrated with 5 volumes of 8M urea lysis buffer at pH 8, sedimented at 3000 rpm for 4 minutes at 4 ° C, and allowed to cool to room temperature with HC110-R protein supernatant with gentle stirring. For 20 minutes. After centrifugation again, the resin was washed three times with 10 volumes of 8M urea lysis buffer, pH 8, with slow stirring at room temperature for 10 minutes, and centrifuged again. After the last washing step, the pellet was taken up in 1 ml of 8M urea lysis buffer and used for loading on the column; the latter was washed twice with 3 volumes of 8M urea lysis buffer and imidazole-containing 8M urea lysis Eluted with buffer and fractionated into several fractions of 150 μl each. The amount of fusion protein in the fraction is determined by gel analysis and Bradford protein assay.
[0187]

15. Amino acid sequence analysis
In order to confirm the amino acid sequence deduced from the cDNA full-length clone HC110-R, the 3 ′ end containing 688 bp ((positions 2486 to 3182)) containing an upstream initiation codon and a Kozak sequence was inserted into a pRSET B expression vector. And cloned into competent BL21 (DE3) pLysSE. Expression of the 21 kD protein (189 AA) in E. coli cells was induced by adding 1 mM IPTG. The fusion protein expressed with this N-terminal His tag was concentrated in a Talon matrix, concentrated in a Centricon tube, and desalted. Due to the N-terminal His tag, sequence analysis of the partial C-terminal protein of the 1 nM 21 kD HC110-R protein was performed by a stepwise Schlack-Kumpf digestion of a variant of Boyd (Boyd et al., 1992) by TopLab (Martinsried). Schlack et al., 1926). Sequence analysis of the removed amino acids was performed on a PROCISE 492 amino acid sequence analyzer (PE Applied Biosystems, Weiterstadt) and analyzed using a PROCISE C reverse phase HPLC system consisting of an ABI 140C micro gradient system and an ABI 785A UV / VIS detector. Identification was performed using PROCISE C control software and ABI data analysis software.
[0189]
First, 25 pmol of the 21 kD HC110-R protein was digested with 2% trypsin (Roche Molecular Biochemicals, Mannheim) at 37 ° C. overnight. A total of four peptide fragments were selected by comparing the chromatogram of the digest without trypsin to the HC110-R standard chromatogram after trypsin digestion to rule out sequence analysis of tryptic autolysates. These four peptide fragments were subjected to protein sequence analysis of the N-terminal part by a stepwise Edman digestion method modified by TopLab (Martinsried) by Hunkapiller et al., (1983). Degraded peptide fragments were separated and fractionated by HPLC. The peptide fraction blotted with Immobilon was transferred to a reaction chamber of a PROCISE 492 amino acid sequence analyzer (Applied Biosystems, Weiterstadt), and the amino acids were analyzed using a 140 C-PTH-analyzer and a UV detector 785 A (Applied Biosystems, Waters). And separated. Amino acids were quantified by reversed-phase HPLC and identified by comparing retention times with a standard chromatogram generated prior to sequence analysis.
[0190]

17． Culture of various cell culture systems
The adherent cell lines COS-7 and HEK-293 were placed in a 110 mm tissue culture dish [Greiner, Solingen] at 37 ° C., 5% CO 2 in 10 mL of medium.2And 95% humidity. Cultured cells were maintained by culturing COS-7 and HEK-293 cells in DMEM medium. 3.024 g / l NaHCO3Medium containing 10% FCS, 50 U / ml penicillin and 50 μg / mL streptomycin was warmed to 37 ° C. before use. For COS-7 precultures, they were stored at 4 ° C. for 2 hours and then mechanically separated from the culture dishes using a cell scraper. HEK-293 cells could be separated directly from the bottom of the culture dish using a glass pipette.
[0192]
18. Transient and stable transfection of eukaryotic cells
The non-liposome transfection reagent FuGENE 6 from Roche Molecular Biochemicals (Mannheim) was used to transiently introduce foreign DNA into animal cells (Kurachi et al., 1998). For this purpose, sterile glass slides coated with 1% gelatin were placed in 35 mm tissue culture dishes, which were set up for a later confocal laser scanning microscope, at approximately 0.5-1.5 × 10 5 in 2 ml of medium.5Individual cells were placed. Cells are grown at 37 ° C. with 5% CO 22And 95% humidity overnight. The medium was changed again before transfection. For transfection, 3 μl of FuGENE6 [Roche Molecular Biochemicals] was diluted in 97 μl of serum-free medium and each reaction mixture was incubated for 5 minutes at room temperature. For each mixture, 100 μl of the diluted FuGENE 6 was added dropwise to 2 μg (0.5-1 μg / μl) of plasmid-DNA by pipetting, mixed carefully, and incubated at room temperature for another 15 minutes. Thereafter, the complete reaction mixture was added dropwise to the cells and the transfection mixture was evenly distributed by gently rotating the dish. Cells were cultured for an additional 1-2 days without changing media. The following three negative controls (negative controls) were included in each transfection: 0.5-1.5 × 10 5 in 35 mm tissue culture dishes6The second culture dish containing cells and not transfected adds DNA to the transfection mixture, but does not add FuGENE 6, and the third culture dish contains FuGENE 6 but no DNA.
[0193]
For stable transfection, the desired plasmid HC110-R was transformed with the expression vector pSecTag A [Invitrogen, Leek, NL] or pIRESneo [Clontech, Palo Alto, U.S.A. S. A. ] With the correct reading frame. These vectors have the resistance gene as a marker so that Zeocin and G418 or Bleomycin 48 are constitutively added 72 hours after transient transfection and at each subsequent medium change. Only cells successfully transfected that express the resistance gene product survive. The optimal concentration of the selective medium containing Zeocin or G418 is predetermined by setting up a dilution series for each cell line.
[0194]
19. Subcellular localization of recombinant proteins in animal cells
To C-terminate the HC110-R protein to GFP (green fluorescent protein), the complete coding region of HC110-R DNA was cloned into the HindIII / SalI site of pEGFP-N3. The 137 kDa fusion protein can be expressed in transiently transfected recombinant cell lines and demonstrated by Western blot analysis. CLSM (confocal laser screening microscopy) shows that the HC110-R-GFP fusion protein is present in the cytoplasm of COS-7 and HEK-293 cells and, to a lesser extent, also localized on the plasma membrane. (See also FIG. 8).
[0195]
The TCS NT with Leica CLSM ("Confocal Laser Scanning Microscope", Leica Lasertechnik, Heidelberg), a Zeiss IM 35 microscope with version 1.5.451 (Zeiss, Oberkochen) was used for the confocal laser scanning microscope. . GFP Protein Fluorescence and Fluorescent Dye Fluorescein isothiocyanate fluorescence was excited at 488 nm using an argon laser, rhodamine, Texas red, phycoerythrin, Alexa 568, LysoTracker.TMRed DND-99, MitoTrackerTMRed CMX Ros and propidium iodide were excited at 568 nm using a krypton laser. The Z series of optical fractions penetrating cells scanned 0.5 μm thick with a resolution of 1024 × 1024 pixels (Giese et al., 1995). The evaluation was performed using AVS software (Advanced Visual Systems Inc., Waltham, Mass., USA), the latter using Adobe Photoshop 5.0 and Corel Draw 8.0 for Windows. Done.
[0196]
Lysotracker probe for labeling acidic organellesTM, The fusion protein is specifically located in the acid lysosome. Particles containing the HC110-R protein showed an increase in number near the nucleic acid. GFP and mouse β2-A fusion protein of an adrenergic GPCR was prepared as a control (accession number X155564, Nakada et al., 1989), and the transfection resulted in the same distribution pattern as in the cell as in the case of the HC110-R-GFP fusion protein. (FIG. 8).

21. HC110-R-MycHis tag construct for stable or transient transfection
The vector pMyc6xHis is obtained by double digesting the vector pSecTagA [Invitrogen, Leak, NL] with the restriction enzymes NhiI and SfiI, blunting the ends, and ligating the vector again. The coding region of HC110-R is a PCR primer P83MycTag_ATG BamHI 5 'primer 5'-ATA GGA TCC TTC GGT TTA ATA CCA ACA TGAGG-3 'and P3058MycTag_o. 25. Binding of PF1022A to HC110-R
Binding of PF1022A and the morpholine derivative BAY44-4400 to HC110-R is demonstrated by SDS-PAGE, ligand preparation and the following analytical flow cytometer (flow cytometry). In addition, PF1022A and its derivatives, like α-LTX, were found to be expressed in HC110-R transfected HEK-293 cells [Ca2+]iTo determine whether it causes a change in HC110-RTX signaling.
[0208]
In some cases, antibodies or proteins that give a clear signal in immunofluorescence may not respond using immunoblotting. Performing SDS-PAGE requires denaturation of the protein, which can destroy conformation-dependent epitopes. Antibodies or proteins that specifically recognize such epitopes can no longer bind. Thus, HC110-R specific binding cannot be identified in Western blots either by using the biotinylated activator PF1022A or by using the more soluble morpholine derivative BAY44-4400 than human PF1022A. BAY44-4400 differs from PF1022A by two morpholine residues covalently linked to the phenyl ring of the D-phenylactyl radical of PF1022A. However, if the SDS is partially removed through disrupting the hydrophobic interaction and the protein is regenerated on an SDS separation gel using urea, detecting HC110-R specific binding in a Western blot Can be. For this purpose, total proteins from untransfected HEK-293 cells and from HEK-293 cells transiently expressing HC110-R-Myc / His; The N-terminal of 54 kDa and the C-terminal of 21 kDa of HC110-R expressed in E. coli were fractionated by SDS-PAGE, regenerated, and blotted by a conventional method. Immunodetection was performed after incubation with ligand BAY44-4400, with rabbit anti-PF1022A-KLJ immune serum, and with goat anti-rabbit IgG HRP antibody. In addition, untransfected HEK-293 cells, HEK-293 cells transiently transfected with HC110-R-Myc / His, and E. coli. the N-terminus of HC110-R expressed in E. coli; A partially regenerated SDS polyacrylamide gel using total proteins from S. contortus was blotted, incubated with PF1022A-biotin, and detected using streptavidin HRP. For each of the two blots, HEK-293 cells stably expressing HC110-R-Myc / His showed a distinct band of 116 kDa in size, whereas lanes using untransfected cells showed this level. No bands are shown. In addition, both the morpholine derivative BAY44-4400 and the biotinylated PF1022A bound to the 54 kDa N-terminus of HC110-R except for the 21 kDa C-terminus show no specific PF1022A binding. Adult H. The total amount of the two bandons of the total protein fraction from C. contortus nematodes can be detected using biotinylated PF1022A: a band of size 110 kDa and another band of size approximately 88 kDa. In particular, the latter is likely to be detected, as is the case with the 83 kDa protein already described for the nematode Heterakis spumosa, since it is detected even when detection is performed exclusively with streptavidin HRP in contrast to the band of size 110 kDa. It is a biotinylated protein. On the other hand, HEK-293 cells stably transfected with HC110-R-Myc / His no longer show a band of size 116 kDa with only streptavidin HRP. Furthermore, non-specific signals generated by the goat anti-rabbit IgG HRP secondary antibody alone could be eliminated.
[0209]
In order to further verify this result, the following ligand precipitation was performed. Aliquots of 2 mg and 4 mg of magnetic Dynal M-280 streptavidin-conjugated beads were mixed with 500 μg of biotinylated PF1022A. In a control mixture using 4 mg of Dynal beads, TST buffer was added instead of PF1022A. Excess PF1022A biotin was removed by magnetic separation. The PF110-R terminus and C terminus expressed in E. coli and previously purified by affinity chromatography were added. After regenerative magnetic separation to remove unbound HC110-R fragment, aliquots obtained from 2 mg and 4 mg of Dynal beads were fractionated by SDS-PAGE and blotted. Detection of the precipitate was performed via an N-terminal fused His tag with mouse anti-His IgG and rabbit anti-mouse IgG HRP antibodies. Based on the fact that the C-terminus of HC110-R that does not bind to PF1022A was previously separated by magnetic separation, only the N-terminal 54 kDa region of HC110-R is precipitated by PF1022A. Non-specific binding of HC110-R N- or C-terminal to streptavidin-conjugated beads was eliminated by not adding biotinylated PF1022A to the reaction mixture.
[0210]
The binding of ligand PF1022A to HC110-R in vivo was further analyzed by FACS analysis (FIG. 13). For this purpose, HEK-293 cells are transiently transfected with HC110-R-GFP or GFP-HC110-R, or otherwise cotransfected with HC110-R-Myc / His and GFP. Was taken. Untransfected HEK-293 cells and β2HEK-293 transiently transfected with -R-GFP or M1-R-GFP was used as a control. Twenty-four hours after transfection, cells were incubated with biotinylated PF1022A and PF1022A-bound cells were detected using streptavidin-phycoerythrin and finally immobilized. Cells transfected with HC110-R-GFP, a negative control, were incubated with only streptavidin-phycoerythrin without PF1022A-biotin.
[0211]
FACScan was used to fluorescence analyze 10,000 HEK-293 cells for cell size, granularity and fluorescent staining, respectively, using an excitation wavelength of 488 mm. Phycoerythrin, like TRITC, has an absorption spectrum that overlaps with EGFP, but the emission spectra are sufficiently far apart to excite both fluorochromes at only a single wavelength. Cell debris can be excluded from fluorescence intensity measurements by providing a "gate" for the main cell population. For quantitative evaluation, the limits for negative (negative), unstained and positive (positive), GFP-fluorescent cells based on untransfected and GFP transfected cells were fixed. The 4.6% green fluorescence (autofluorescence) of untransfected HEK-293 cells was subtracted from other GFP fluorescence samples; and the value of nonspecific staining of cells with phycoerythrin-conjugated streptavidin (5.4%) Was subtracted from all red fluorescent cells (Table 1).

27. Obtaining antibodies
Antibodies were obtained by using female NMRI mice and rabbits (Chinchilla cross). Immunization of NMRI mice was performed by adding 3 × 15 μg of purified 21 kD ΔC-terminal HC110-R protein fragment to 100 μl of PBS together with 100 μl of FCA each.− And injected subcutaneously on days 1, 8 and 15 into two naive NMRI mice. Blood samples were collected and serum was obtained on day 23.
[0219]
To obtain serum, blood obtained by cardiac puncture was first incubated at 37 ° C. for 1 hour and then at 4 ° C. for at least 2 hours. The cell components were then pelleted twice in a Beckman GPKR centrifuge at 3000 rpm for 10 minutes at 4 ° C and the supernatant was inactivated at 56 ° C for 45 minutes. After further centrifugation at 13,000 rpm, 4 ° C. for 10 minutes in Heraeus biofuge 15R, the serum can be removed and stored at −20 ° C. until further use.
[0220]
After the initial blood collection and obtaining pre-immune serum, two rabbits are first given an equal volume of PBS.−50 μg of the C-terminal 21 kD HC110-R protein and 50 μg of the 54 kD N-terminal HC110-R protein in a suspension consisting of and FCA were administered by subcutaneous injection. On day 31 and day 79 after the first immunization, two more immunizations with 100 μg of antigen were performed. The first blood collection was performed on day 43. A second blood draw and serum was obtained on day 98 after the first immunization.
[0221]

The α-LTX concentrations (0, 7.5, 25, 50, 75, 90 and 120 nM) for the (second peak, black line) were plotted on the vertical axis.

FIG. 13. Detection of PF1022A binding to HC110-R transfected HEK-293 cells by FACScan.
Untransfected GFP, HC110-R-GFP, GFP-HC110-R, β25 × 10 5 transiently transfected with -R-GFP and M1-R-GFP and transiently co-transfected with HC110-R-Myc / His5 In each case of HEK-293 cells, after transfection, they were incubated with 0.5 μg / mL PF1022A-biotin and streptavidin-phycoerythrin (1: 300) for 24 hours and fixed. After the subtraction, GFP fluorescent cells bound to PF1022A (GFP, HC110-R-GFP, GFP-HC110-R, β2-R-GFP, M1-R-GFP and HC110-R-Myc / His + GFP) ratios were found (PF1022A binding in%). The average of triplicate mixtures was determined and the standard deviation was determined.
